  /** Converts a <button> to look like an <a> tag. */
  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;
    border: 0;

    color: var(--chops-link-color);
    text-decoration: none;

  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */
    display: inline-flex;
    align-items: center;

    text-decoration: none;

  a.button:hover, .button:hover {

  textarea, select, input {
    box-sizing: border-box;

  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





After invoke requestFullScreen and append multiple option to select element, when browser goes into fullscreen and tab temporarily unresponsive, interestingly the fullscreen notification toast will be overlapped with the black select dropdown menu.



<span class="line"><!---->After invoke requestFullScreen and append multiple option to select element, when browser goes into fullscreen and tab temporarily unresponsive, interestingly the fullscreen notification toast will be overlapped with the black select dropdown menu.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I able to reproduce the overlap fullscreen toast on Linux distro including Ubuntu, Debian and Arch Linux (KDE).



<span class="line"><!---->I able to reproduce the overlap fullscreen toast on Linux distro including Ubuntu, Debian and Arch Linux (KDE).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





- Chromium 100.0.4896.127 (Official Build) Arch Linux (64-bit)



<span class="line"><!---->- Chromium 100.0.4896.127 (Official Build) Arch Linux (64-bit)<!----></span>



<br>





- Chrome 100.0.4896.127 (Official Build) (64-bit) on Ubuntu 21.10 (X11 and Wayland)



<span class="line"><!---->- Chrome 100.0.4896.127 (Official Build) (64-bit) on Ubuntu 21.10 (X11 and Wayland)<!----></span>



<br>





- Chrome Dev 102.0.4997.0 (Official Build) dev (64-bit) on Ubuntu 21.10 (X11 and Wayland)



<span class="line"><!---->- Chrome Dev 102.0.4997.0 (Official Build) dev (64-bit) on Ubuntu 21.10 (X11 and Wayland)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





1. Visit attached testcase.html



<span class="line"><!---->1. Visit attached testcase.html<!----></span>



<br>





2. Click anywhere on the page



<span class="line"><!---->2. Click anywhere on the page<!----></span>



<br>





3. Fullscreen notification toast will be overlapped by black select dropdown menu



<span class="line"><!---->3. Fullscreen notification toast will be overlapped by black select dropdown menu<!----></span>



<br>





(If the testcase doesn't work as on PoC video, try to change the selectElement[641811] array index to lower or higher value)



<span class="line"><!---->(If the testcase doesn't work as on PoC video, try to change the selectElement[641811] array index to lower or higher value)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<b class="line"><!---->CREDIT INFORMATION<!----></b>

<span class="line"><!---->Reporter credit: Irvan Kurniawan (sourc7)<!----></span>

I'm not sure if it's feasible to fix this on Linux.  The "Press <esc> to exit fullscreen" bubble isn't a native window, so things like right-click menus or select dropdowns will cover it.  We can make it a native window by removing `params.parent` in [1], but we have little control over how the window manager will stack the windows.  Even less so on Wayland.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm not sure if it's feasible to fix this on Linux.  The "Press &lt;esc&gt; to exit fullscreen" bubble isn't a native window, so things like right-click menus or select dropdowns will cover it.  We can make it a native window by removing `params.parent` in [1], but we have little control over how the window manager will stack the windows.  Even less so on Wayland.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





robliao@ do you have any ideas?



<span class="line"><!---->robliao@ do you have any ideas?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:components/fullscreen_control/fullscreen_control_popup.cc;drc=e5a38eddbdf45d7563a00d019debd11b803af1bb;l=31"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:components/fullscreen_control/fullscreen_control_popup.cc;drc=e5a38eddbdf45d7563a00d019debd11b803af1bb;l=31<!----></a>

re c#8:  It's not creating a native window because of this:



<span class="line"><!---->re c#8:  It's not creating a native window because of this:<!----></span>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/chrome_views_delegate_linux.cc;drc=edab26bf11e993e5069d433e8c2186ad2dee012e;l=45



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/chrome_views_delegate_linux.cc;drc=edab26bf11e993e5069d433e8c2186ad2dee012e;l=45"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/chrome_views_delegate_linux.cc;drc=edab26bf11e993e5069d433e8c2186ad2dee012e;l=45<!----></a>



<br>





It will create a NativeWidgetAura instead of a DesktopNativeWidgetAura.



<span class="line"><!---->It will create a NativeWidgetAura instead of a DesktopNativeWidgetAura.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Anyway, even if it is a native window, it doesn't help to solve this issue for Linux.



<span class="line"><!---->Anyway, even if it is a native window, it doesn't help to solve this issue for Linux.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Also adding ChromeOS based on c#9.



<span class="line"><!---->Also adding ChromeOS based on c#9.<!----></span>

Sorry thomasanderson@, security bugs can't lurk unassigned in the backlog. We need to drive it to conclusion:



<span class="line"><!---->Sorry thomasanderson@, security bugs can't lurk unassigned in the backlog. We need to drive it to conclusion:<!----></span>



<br>





a) a fix, even if it's multiple quarters of work and involves getting it on OKRs (if the whole Linux window structure needs redesign)



<span class="line"><!---->a) a fix, even if it's multiple quarters of work and involves getting it on OKRs (if the whole Linux window structure needs redesign)<!----></span>



<br>





b) declare that this can't be fixed, which might require us to take extreme measures such as removing full-screen mode on Linux.



<span class="line"><!---->b) declare that this can't be fixed, which might require us to take extreme measures such as removing full-screen mode on Linux.<!----></span>



<br>





c) determine that this, somehow, can't be used as an effective spoof, for example because the black box is always so huge that it wouldn't allow an attacker to draw a realistic spoof browser.



<span class="line"><!---->c) determine that this, somehow, can't be used as an effective spoof, for example because the black box is always so huge that it wouldn't allow an attacker to draw a realistic spoof browser.<!----></span>

Re c#14: I believe this is (c) an effective spoof



<span class="line"><!---->Re c#14: I believe this is (c) an effective spoof<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Reason: The bubble being covered (which just says "press ESC to exit fullscreen") appears over the web contents.  So the page can just create an identical-looking bubble and display any text they want (which is effectively a much better spoof than covering).  Additionally, I don't think it's a spoof to cover "press ESC to exit fullscreen".  Firefox, for example, doesn't even show a message when entering fullscreen.



<span class="line"><!---->Reason: The bubble being covered (which just says "press ESC to exit fullscreen") appears over the web contents.  So the page can just create an identical-looking bubble and display any text they want (which is effectively a much better spoof than covering).  Additionally, I don't think it's a spoof to cover "press ESC to exit fullscreen".  Firefox, for example, doesn't even show a message when entering fullscreen.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is also (b) infeasible to fix on Linux (see 



<span class="line"><!---->This is also (b) infeasible to fix on Linux (see <!----></span>





comment#7



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c7"><!---->comment#7<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





adetaylor: please let me know if you agree and we can close this issue.



<span class="line"><!---->adetaylor: please let me know if you agree and we can close this issue.<!----></span>

The select element width can be resized so it can only cover the fullscreen notification bubble. 



<span class="line"><!---->The select element width can be resized so it can only cover the fullscreen notification bubble. <!----></span>

> Reason: The bubble being covered (which just says "press ESC to exit fullscreen") appears over the web contents.  So the page can just create an identical-looking bubble and display any text they want (which is effectively a much better spoof than covering).  Additionally, I don't think it's a spoof to cover "press ESC to exit fullscreen".  Firefox, for example, doesn't even show a message when entering fullscreen.



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; Reason: The bubble being covered (which just says "press ESC to exit fullscreen") appears over the web contents.  So the page can just create an identical-looking bubble and display any text they want (which is effectively a much better spoof than covering). Firefox is showing fullscreen notification spoof "permission.site is now full screen" with button "Exit Fullscreen (Esc)" following the WhatWG Fullscreen API Standard 



<span class="line"><!---->Firefox is showing fullscreen notification spoof "permission.site is now full screen" with button "Exit Fullscreen (Esc)" following the WhatWG Fullscreen API Standard <!----></span>





https://fullscreen.spec.whatwg.org/#security-and-privacy-considerations



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://fullscreen.spec.whatwg.org/#security-and-privacy-considerations"><!---->https://fullscreen.spec.whatwg.org/#security-and-privacy-considerations<!----></a>





 "User agents should ensure, e.g. by means of an overlay, that the end user is aware something is displayed fullscreen...". I've also reported several full-screen notification spoofs to Firefox in the past e.g.

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
